     <p>The <b>University of Oregon</b> (<b>UO</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/State_university_system" title="State university system">public</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coeducation" title="Coeducation" class="mw-redirect">coeducational</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eugene,_Oregon" title="Eugene, Oregon">Eugene, Oregon</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. UO was founded in 1876 and graduated its first class two years later.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/The_Carnegie_Foundation_for_the_Advancement_of_Teaching" title="The Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching" class="mw-redirect">Carnegie Foundation</a> classifies the University of Oregon as a Tier 1 RU/VH (very high research activity) university.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> It is one of 108 universities to have such a designation. Additionally, the UO is one of only two <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> members in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AAU_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAU-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As the <a href="/wiki/Flagship_campus" title="Flagship campus" class="mw-redirect">flagship</a> university of the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_University_System" title="Oregon University System">Oregon University System</a>, the UO is one of the nation's premier public teaching and research universities.<sup id="cite_ref-AboutUO_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AboutUO-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The current UO student body is composed of students from all 50 of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" title="District of Columbia" class="mw-redirect">District of Columbia</a>, two U.S. territories, and 89 countries around the world. As of Fall 2012, UO offers 269 degree programs, including highly nationally-ranked graduate programs in <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">Biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">Business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Law" title="Environmental Law" class="mw-redirect">Environmental Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geological_Sciences" title="Geological Sciences" class="mw-redirect">Geological Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">Psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sports_Marketing" title="Sports Marketing" class="mw-redirect">Sports Marketing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Design" title="Sustainable Design" class="mw-redirect">Sustainable Design</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-UOSnapshot_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UOSnapshot-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UO_campus_profile_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UO_campus_profile-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of March 2012, University of Oregon faculty and alumni include two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> recipients, 10 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, 19 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_scholars" title="Rhodes scholars" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes scholars</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Scholarship" title="Marshall Scholarship">Marshall scholars</a>, 58 <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Fellowship" title="Guggenheim Fellowship">Guggenheim Fellows</a>, and 129 <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_scholars" title="Fulbright scholars" class="mw-redirect">Fulbright scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

             </ul> </li> 
           </ul> </li>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_early_years">The early years</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The early years">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:1893_Class_Marker,_University_of_Oregon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1893_Class_Marker%2C_University_of_Oregon.jpg/220px-1893_Class_Marker%2C_University_of_Oregon.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1893_Class_Marker%2C_University_of_Oregon.jpg/330px-1893_Class_Marker%2C_University_of_Oregon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1893_Class_Marker%2C_University_of_Oregon.jpg/440px-1893_Class_Marker%2C_University_of_Oregon.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:1893_Class_Marker,_University_of_Oregon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 1893 Class Marker, near Villard Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_Legislature" title="Oregon State Legislature" class="mw-redirect">Oregon State Legislature</a> established the university on October 12, 1872, despite the new state's funding woes.<sup id="cite_ref-125AnnivEarly_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125AnnivEarly-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The residents of Eugene struggled to help finance the institution, holding numerous fundraising events such as strawberry festivals, church socials, and produce sales. In total they raised $27,500, enough to buy eighteen acres of land at a cost of $2500.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The doors officially opened in 1876, with <a href="/wiki/Deady_Hall" title="Deady Hall">Deady Hall</a> its sole building. The first year of enrollment contained 155 students taught by five faculty members. The first graduating class was in 1878, graduating five students.<sup id="cite_ref-125AnnivEarly_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125AnnivEarly-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1881, the university was nearly closed, it was $8,000 in debt before <a href="/wiki/Henry_Villard" title="Henry Villard">Henry Villard</a> donated $7,000 toward to help pay for the debt.<sup id="cite_ref-125AnnivEarly_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125AnnivEarly-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1913, and again in 1932, there were proposals to merge the university with what is now referred to as <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_University" title="Oregon State University">Oregon State University</a>. Evidently, both proposals were defeated.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maturity_as_a_university">Maturity as a university</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Maturity as a university">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>During Prince Lucien Campbell's tenure as president from 1902 to 1925, the university experienced tremendous growth compared to its early years. The budget, enrollment, facilities, and faculty members all grew several times its amount prior to his presidency. Numerous schools were also established during his tenure, including the School of Music in 1902, the School of Education in 1910, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_School_of_Architecture_and_Allied_Arts" title="University of Oregon School of Architecture and Allied Arts">School of Architecture</a>, the College of Business in 1914, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_School_of_Law" title="University of Oregon School of Law">School of Law</a> in 1915, the School of Journalism in 1916, and the School of Health and Physical Education in 1920.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Oregon_ducks_football_1916.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Oregon_ducks_football_1916.jpg/220px-Oregon_ducks_football_1916.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Oregon_ducks_football_1916.jpg/330px-Oregon_ducks_football_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Oregon_ducks_football_1916.jpg/440px-Oregon_ducks_football_1916.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Oregon_ducks_football_1916.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> University of Oregon 1917 football team
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>However, the University of Oregon lost its School of Engineering to <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Agricultural_College" title="Oregon Agricultural College" class="mw-redirect">Oregon Agricultural College</a>, now known as <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_University" title="Oregon State University">Oregon State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125AnnivBoom_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125AnnivBoom-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Zorn-MacPherson Bill in 1932 proposed that the University of Oregon and <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_College" title="Oregon State College" class="mw-redirect">Oregon State College</a> (now &quot;University&quot;), to be merged into one university. The bill lost in a landslide vote of over 6 to 1.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Oregon Medical School was originally founded in 1887 in Portland and later merged with <a href="/wiki/Willamette_University" title="Willamette University">Willamette University</a>'s program in 1913. However, in 1974 it officially became an independent institution known as <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Health_Sciences_University" title="Oregon Health Sciences University" class="mw-redirect">Oregon Health Sciences University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1969, the UO was admitted into the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>.</p> 
     <p>With financial support from the state dwindling from 40% to 13% of the university budget,<sup id="cite_ref-OQTransformers_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OQTransformers-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> in January 2001, University President <a href="/wiki/Dave_Frohnmayer" title="Dave Frohnmayer" class="mw-redirect">Dave Frohnmayer</a> began Campaign Oregon with the goal of raising $600 million by December 2008, the greatest philanthropic fundraising campaign in the history of the state of Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> With total contributions exceeding $100 million from benefactors such as <a href="/wiki/Phil_Knight" title="Phil Knight">Phil Knight</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lorry_I._Lokey" title="Lorry I. Lokey">Lorry I. Lokey</a>, the campaign goal was exceeded by over $253 million.<sup id="cite_ref-OQTransformers_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OQTransformers-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Push_for_independence_and_growth">Push for independence and growth</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Push for independence and growth">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Dalai_Lama_Visit_(Eugene,_Oregon)-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Dalai_Lama_Visit_%28Eugene%2C_Oregon%29-2.jpg/220px-Dalai_Lama_Visit_%28Eugene%2C_Oregon%29-2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Dalai_Lama_Visit_%28Eugene%2C_Oregon%29-2.jpg/330px-Dalai_Lama_Visit_%28Eugene%2C_Oregon%29-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Dalai_Lama_Visit_%28Eugene%2C_Oregon%29-2.jpg/440px-Dalai_Lama_Visit_%28Eugene%2C_Oregon%29-2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Dalai_Lama_Visit_(Eugene,_Oregon)-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Knight_Arena" title="Matthew Knight Arena">Matthew Knight Arena</a> hosting the 
        <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">14th Dalai Lama</a> in 2013
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University occupies 80 buildings. However, there are also many ongoing construction projects,<sup id="cite_ref-UO_campus_profile_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UO_campus_profile-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> which are expected to help accommodate an increase in total undergraduate enrollment.</p> 
     <p>There is currently a growing movement to establish an independent university board.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Proponents believe an independent board will give the university more autonomy, and free it from relying on inadequate state funding. Additionally, it is believed that an independent board will help pave the way for a new $1.6 billion dollar endowment.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On March 31, 2012, a <a href="/wiki/Political_Action_Committee" title="Political Action Committee" class="mw-redirect">Political Action Committee</a> called Oregonians For Higher Education Excellence was formed by <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Sportswear" title="Columbia Sportswear">Columbia Sportswear</a> CEO Tim Boyle.<sup id="cite_ref-PAC_transactions_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAC_transactions-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> As of May 23, 2012, the organization has raised over $320,000. Notable contributors to the PAC include, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Knight" title="Phil Knight">Phil Knight</a>, Patrick Kilkenny, and Tim Boyle. According to Boyle, the PAC will help facilitate an increase in autonomy at the University of Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-New_PAC_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_PAC-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On August 1, 2012, former provost and executive vice-chancellor of <a href="/wiki/UC_Irvine" title="UC Irvine" class="mw-redirect">UC Irvine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_R._Gottfredson" title="Michael R. Gottfredson">Michael R. Gottfredson</a> took over as president of the University of Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> He was the sole finalist for the position.<sup id="cite_ref-Finalist_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Finalist-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Gottfredson succeeded interim president <a href="/wiki/Robert_M._Berdahl" title="Robert M. Berdahl">Robert M. Berdahl</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Institution">Institution</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Institution">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table class="infobox vcard" style="width: 22em">
