     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_schools">Colleges and schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Colleges and schools">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Oregon is organized into eight schools and colleges—six professional schools and colleges, an Arts and Sciences College and an Honors College.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Architecture_and_Allied_Arts">School of Architecture and Allied Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: School of Architecture and Allied Arts">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_School_of_Architecture_and_Allied_Arts" title="University of Oregon School of Architecture and Allied Arts">School of Architecture and Allied Arts</a> (called &quot;triple-A&quot; or &quot;AAA&quot;) was founded by <a href="/wiki/Ellis_F._Lawrence" title="Ellis F. Lawrence">Ellis F. Lawrence</a> in 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The school offers undergraduate and graduate degrees in architecture, art, including digital arts, arts and administration, art history, historic preservation, interior architecture, landscape architecture, and planning, public policy and management, and product design. The school also offers an architectural program, digital arts program, and product design program in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>.</p> 
     <p>The school offers the only accredited degree in architecture, landscape architecture, and interior architecture in Oregon. The <a href="/wiki/National_Architectural_Accrediting_Board" title="National Architectural Accrediting Board">National Architectural Accrediting Board</a> accredits both the undergraduate bachelor of architecture five-year degree and the master of architecture. Other nationally accredited degrees include the planning and public administration, landscape architecture, and interior architecture programs. The undergraduate architecture program is consistently ranked among the highest in the country, and is currently ranked as the #1 public program for &quot;Sustainable Design Practice and Principles&quot; by <i>DesignIntelligence</i> magazine.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="College_of_Arts_and_Sciences">College of Arts and Sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: College of Arts and Sciences">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UO_Gilbert_FrontDetail.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/UO_Gilbert_FrontDetail.jpg/220px-UO_Gilbert_FrontDetail.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/UO_Gilbert_FrontDetail.jpg/330px-UO_Gilbert_FrontDetail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/UO_Gilbert_FrontDetail.jpg/440px-UO_Gilbert_FrontDetail.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UO_Gilbert_FrontDetail.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Detail of the decoration over the front entrance to Gilbert Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The College of Arts and Sciences (CAS) covers a large array of departments in the arts and sciences. The creative writing graduate program is nationally recognized as being among the best in the nation—fewer than two percent are admitted out of 700+ applicants each year.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Charles_H._Lundquist_College_of_Business">Charles H. Lundquist College of Business</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Charles H. Lundquist College of Business">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The Charles H. Lundquist College of Business (LCB) was founded in 1884 and offers courses in fields such as accounting, decision sciences, entrepreneurship, finance, management, and marketing. It is also home to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon_Investment_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="University of Oregon Investment Group (page does not exist)">University of Oregon Investment Group</a> and the Warsaw Sports Marketing Center, one of the first programs to offer an M.B.A. in sports business<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> and is noted as having the best sports business and marketing programs in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Each year, the college's Lundquist Center for Entrepreneurship presents the <a href="/wiki/New_Venture_Championship" title="New Venture Championship">New Venture Championship</a>, an investment competition for graduate students that draws competitors from all over the world. The College is housed in the <a href="/wiki/Lillis_Business_Complex" title="Lillis Business Complex">Lillis Business Complex</a>. The college's current dean is Cornelis A. “Kees” de Kluyver, who is himself an alumnus, having earned a bachelor’s degree in marketing and a master of business administration degree from the University of Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-deKluyver_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deKluyver-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Dean de Kluyver assumed his duties on September 1, 2010, taking over from Dennis Howard, who completed a two-year appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-deKluyver_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deKluyver-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="College_of_Education">College of Education</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: College of Education">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The College of Education was established in 1896 as a branch of the Department of Philosophy and later merged with the Department of Science and Arts in 1900. It wasn't until 1910 that the School of Education was established as an independent college. In 1908, this college was accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Commission_on_Colleges_and_Universities" title="Northwest Commission on Colleges and Universities">Northwest Association of Colleges and Secondary Schools</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the U.S. News &amp; World Report 2009 edition of &quot;America’s Best Graduate Schools,&quot; the College of Education ranked 4th overall and 1st among public universities.<sup id="cite_ref-OPBEduRanking_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OPBEduRanking-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> For the 4th consecutive year, the UO special education program ranked third in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-OPBEduRanking_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OPBEduRanking-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Robert_D._Clark_Honors_College">Robert D. Clark Honors College</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Robert D. Clark Honors College">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Clark_Honors_College" title="Robert D. Clark Honors College">Robert D. Clark Honors College</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Clark Honors College is a small college intended to complement the existing majors already in place at the university by joining select students and faculty for a low student to teacher ratio (25:1 maximum).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> For Fall 2011 Term, 1570 students applied and 205 students entered. The mean Grade point average [GPA] of admitted students was 3.93, and the mean Scholastic Aptitude Test [SAT, Reading + Math only] score was 1360 (97th/98th percentile).</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Journalism_and_Communication">School of Journalism and Communication</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: School of Journalism and Communication">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The School of Journalism and Communication is one of the oldest journalism schools in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Journalism_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Journalism-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> It began as a department in 1912, and became a professional school 1916. It has the accreditation of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Accrediting_Council_for_Education_in_Journalism_and_Mass_Communication&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Accrediting Council for Education in Journalism and Mass Communication (page does not exist)">Accrediting Council for Education in Journalism and Mass Communication</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ACEJMC_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACEJMC-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> It currently runs <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://flux.uoregon.edu">Flux</a></i> magazine, a student-produced, award-winning publication.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Eight of the nine <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners from the University of Oregon graduated from the School of Journalism and Communication.<sup id="cite_ref-pulitzer_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pulitzer-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> It also awards the annual <a href="/wiki/Payne_Award_for_Ethics_in_Journalism" title="Payne Award for Ethics in Journalism">Payne Award for Ethics in Journalism</a>. Allen Hall, the new home of the SOJC, was officially opened on March 3, 2013.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Law">School of Law</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: School of Law">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_School_of_Law" title="University of Oregon School of Law">University of Oregon School of Law</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_School_of_Law" title="University of Oregon School of Law">School of Law</a> was formed in 1884 in Portland and relocated to Eugene in early 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-UO_history_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UO_history-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> It was admitted into the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Law_Schools" title="Association of American Law Schools">Association of American Law Schools</a> in 1919 and received accreditation from the <a href="/wiki/American_Bar_Association" title="American Bar Association">American Bar Association</a> in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Music_and_Dance">School of Music and Dance</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: School of Music and Dance">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The School of Music and Dance was initially just the Department of Music in 1886, and developed into the School of Music in 1900. It was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Schools_of_Music" title="National Association of Schools of Music">National Association of Schools of Music</a> in 1928. The school offers over 20 ensembles in vocal and instrumental music, giving approximately 200 public performances a year.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Renamed in 2006, the <a href="/wiki/MarAbel_B._Frohnmayer_Music_Building" title="MarAbel B. Frohnmayer Music Building">MarAbel B. Frohnmayer Music Building</a> is the physical home of the school, named after former University of Oregon <a href="/wiki/David_B._Frohnmayer" title="David B. Frohnmayer">President Frohnmayer</a>'s mother, a 1932 alumna of the School.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Beall Concert Hall, the primary performance hall within the school, was designed by Ellis F. Lawrence.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Oregon_Bach_Festival">Oregon Bach Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Oregon Bach Festival">edit</a>]</span></h5> 
     <p>The UO is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Bach_Festival" title="Oregon Bach Festival">Oregon Bach Festival</a>, a donor-supported program of the University and the only major music festival affiliated with an American university. Founded in 1970 by German conductor <a href="/wiki/Helmuth_Rilling" title="Helmuth Rilling">Helmuth Rilling</a> and UO professor (and past president of the <a href="/wiki/American_Choral_Directors_Association" title="American Choral Directors Association">American Choral Directors Association</a>) Royce Saltzman, the festival has grown into an international program that draws hundreds of musicians and over 40,000 attendees annually. The festival's focus is choral and orchestral music, and it hosts a professional choir and orchestra each year to perform major works by <a href="/wiki/Bach" title="Bach" class="mw-redirect">Bach</a> and other composers; it also sponsors a master class in conducting that draws participants from around the world.</p> 
     <p>The festival has presented such artists as <a href="/wiki/Frederica_von_Stade" title="Frederica von Stade">Frederica von Stade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_McFerrin" title="Bobby McFerrin">Bobby McFerrin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garrison_Keillor" title="Garrison Keillor">Garrison Keillor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Quasthoff" title="Thomas Quasthoff">Thomas Quasthoff</a>, who made his American debut in Eugene in 1995. The festival actively commissions and premieres new choral-orchestra works, including pieces by <a href="/wiki/Arvo_P%C3%A4rt" title="Arvo P&auml;rt">Arvo P&auml;rt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osvaldo_Golijov" title="Osvaldo Golijov">Osvaldo Golijov</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tan_Dun" title="Tan Dun">Tan Dun</a>. A Bach Festival recording of the world-premiere performance of <a href="/wiki/Krzyztof_Penderecki" title="Krzyztof Penderecki" class="mw-redirect">Krzyztof Penderecki</a>'s <i>Credo</i> won the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> for best choral performance.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_campus" title="University of Oregon campus" class="mw-redirect">University of Oregon campus</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Lillis_Complex_(University_of_Oregon).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Lillis_Complex_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg/220px-Lillis_Complex_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Lillis_Complex_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg/330px-Lillis_Complex_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Lillis_Complex_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg/440px-Lillis_Complex_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lillis_Complex_(University_of_Oregon).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Lillis Complex (University of Oregon)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The campus is spread over 295 acres (119&nbsp;ha) and holds sixty major buildings,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as providing a home for more than 500 varieties of trees.<sup id="cite_ref-TreeAtlas_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TreeAtlas-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Eugene is located near many prominent geographic features such as the <a href="/wiki/Willamette_River" title="Willamette River">Willamette River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. Also within a two-hour drive is the <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland</a> metropolitan area.</p> 
     <p>Based on Ellis F. Lawrence's vision, many of the university's buildings are planned around several major quadrangles, many of which abut the 13th Avenue pedestrian mall.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is known for being the site of a pioneering participatory planning experiment known as the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Experiment" title="Oregon Experiment" class="mw-redirect">Oregon Experiment</a>, which is also the subject of a book of the same name that evolved into the well known book <i><a href="/wiki/A_Pattern_Language" title="A Pattern Language">A Pattern Language</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Alexander" title="Christopher Alexander">Christopher Alexander</a>. The two major principles of the project are that buildings should be designed, in part, by the people who will ultimately use them with the help of an &quot;architect facilitator&quot;, and that construction should occur over many small projects as opposed to a few large ones.</p> 
     <p>Although academic buildings are spread throughout the campus, the majority are located along East 13th Avenue, with heavy pedestrian traffic at the intersection with Kincaid Street.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Student recreation and union centers are located toward the center of the campus, with residence halls on the east side of campus. Sports facilities are grouped in the southern-central part of campus with the <a href="/wiki/Autzen_Stadium" title="Autzen Stadium">Autzen Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/PK_Park" title="PK Park">PK Park</a> complexes across the Willamette River. The university also owns and operates several satellite facilities, including a large facility in the White Stag Block of downtown Portland.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_campus_and_memorial_quad">Old campus and memorial quad</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Old campus and memorial quad">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:DeadyHallWest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/DeadyHallWest.jpg/220px-DeadyHallWest.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/DeadyHallWest.jpg/330px-DeadyHallWest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/DeadyHallWest.jpg/440px-DeadyHallWest.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:DeadyHallWest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Deady Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The oldest section of campus is located in the northwest area of the current campus. The university’s first building, <a href="/wiki/Deady_Hall" title="Deady Hall">Deady Hall</a>, opened on October 16, 1876, when the University had an enrollment of 177 students. It was originally known as “the building” before being named after Judge Matthew Deady in 1893. The second building on campus is known as <a href="/wiki/Villard_Hall" title="Villard Hall">Villard Hall</a> and is home to the Theater Arts and Comparative Literature Departments. Completed in 1886, the hall was named after railroad magnate <a href="/wiki/Henry_Villard" title="Henry Villard">Henry Villard</a>, who provided financial aid to the university in 1881. Before its naming, it was known as “the new building.” Both Deady and Villard Halls were designated <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmarks</a> in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-Deady_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deady-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Just south of Old Campus is the Memorial Quad, which runs north and south along Kincaid Street, capped at both ends by the main campus library, <a href="/wiki/Knight_Library" title="Knight Library">Knight Library</a>, on the south side, and the <a href="/wiki/Lillis_Business_Complex" title="Lillis Business Complex">Lillis Business Complex</a> on the north. It is flanked on the west by the tallest building on campus, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Lucien_Campbell_Hall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Prince Lucien Campbell Hall (page does not exist)">Prince Lucien Campbell Hall</a>, also known as “PLC,”, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Condon_Hall_(University_of_Oregon)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Condon Hall (University of Oregon) (page does not exist)">Condon Hall</a> on the west, housing the Geography department, and the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Schnitzer_Museum_of_Art" title="Jordan Schnitzer Museum of Art">Jordan Schnitzer Museum of Art</a> on the east, which was remodeled and reopened on January 23, 2005. Also adjacent to Memorial Quad is Chapman Hall, which houses the <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Clark_Honors_College" title="Robert D. Clark Honors College">Robert D. Clark Honors College</a>.<br style="clear:both;" /></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_campus">Central campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Central campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:JohnsonHallUO.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/JohnsonHallUO.JPG/220px-JohnsonHallUO.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/JohnsonHallUO.JPG/330px-JohnsonHallUO.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/JohnsonHallUO.JPG/440px-JohnsonHallUO.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JohnsonHallUO.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Johnson Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The center of campus houses a mixture of academic buildings, an administration building, and student recreation buildings. Just to the east of Memorial Quad, facing 13th Avenue is <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Hall_(Eugene,_Oregon)" title="Johnson Hall (Eugene, Oregon)">Johnson Hall</a> where offices for higher administration and trustee offices are found, including the offices of the University President. Directly across 13th Avenue, facing Johnson Hall is the Pioneer statue, a likeness of a bearded, buckskin-clad pioneer cast in bronze by sculptor <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Phimister_Proctor" title="Alexander Phimister Proctor">Alexander Phimister Proctor</a> in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1932, Proctor's &quot;Pioneer Mother&quot; statue was dedicated in the Women's Memorial Quadrangle on the other side of Johnson Hall; the two statues are aligned so that they can &quot;see&quot; one another through the large windows of the hall's main floor.</p> 
     <p>Lawrence Hall is located at the end of hardscape walkway, directly north of the intersection of 13th Avenue and University Street. It houses the School of Architecture and Allied Arts and is named after its first Dean, <a href="/wiki/Ellis_F._Lawrence" title="Ellis F. Lawrence">Ellis F. Lawrence</a> in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Allen Hall, opened in 1954, is located adjacent to Lawrence Hall and houses the School of Journalism and Communication.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Additionally, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Erb_Memorial_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Erb Memorial Union (page does not exist)">Erb Memorial Union</a> and the recreation center are situated in this part of campus.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lorry_I._Lokey_Science_Complex_and_east_campus">Lorry I. Lokey Science Complex and east campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Lorry I. Lokey Science Complex and east campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Willamette-Hall-UO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Willamette-Hall-UO.jpg/220px-Willamette-Hall-UO.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Willamette-Hall-UO.jpg/330px-Willamette-Hall-UO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Willamette-Hall-UO.jpg/440px-Willamette-Hall-UO.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Willamette-Hall-UO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Willamette Hall, the centerpiece of the Physics department
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Lorry I. Lokey Science Complex comprises multiple science buildings to the east of Lawrence Hall, on the north side of 13th Avenue. Willamette Hall's <a href="/wiki/Paul_Olum" title="Paul Olum">Paul Olum</a> Atrium is the center of the university's hard sciences complex. The construction of the $45.6 million additions of <a href="/wiki/Willamette_Hall" title="Willamette Hall">Willamette Hall</a>, home of the physics department; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cascade_Hall_(University_of_Oregon)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cascade Hall (University of Oregon) (page does not exist)">Cascade</a>, home of the geology department; <a href="/wiki/Deschutes_Hall" title="Deschutes Hall">Deschutes Hall</a>, home of the computer science department; and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Streisinger_Hall_(University_of_Oregon)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Streisinger Hall (University of Oregon) (page does not exist)">Streisinger</a> Halls to the complex was completed in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Within the Lokey Science Complex are two facilities focused on integrative science.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> One is the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lokey_Laboratories&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lokey Laboratories (page does not exist)">Lokey Laboratories</a>, which is a shared-use facility with state-of-the-art characterization instrumentation. Lokey Laboratories is associated with the Oregon Nanoscience and Microtechnologies Institute (ONAMI) and was dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Lorry_I._Lokey" title="Lorry I. Lokey">Lorry I. Lokey</a> on February 19, 2008 for his $25 million donation toward the project.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> It is located underground, beneath the quad between Heustis and Deschutes Halls, to minimize vibrations. The newest building, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewis_Integrative_Science_Building&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lewis Integrative Science Building (page does not exist)">Lewis Integrative Science Building</a>, sits at the north end of this quad and opened in the fall of 2012. Immediately to the east of the Lokey Science Complex is Oregon Hall, which houses administrative offices including the Office of the Registrar and Office of Admissions.</p> 
     <p>The northeast corner of campus is home to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ford_Alumni_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ford Alumni Center (page does not exist)">Ford Alumni Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Knight_Arena" title="Matthew Knight Arena">Matthew Knight Arena</a>. The majority of the rest of the eastern part of campus is dedicated to residence halls. Carson Hall, located near the Erb Memorial Union, provides dining services along with dormitories. Just south is the Living-Learning Center, opened in 2006. It is a collection of functions including dormitories, classrooms, study areas, dining rooms, and recreational rooms to provide a single location for many student activities.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The newest residence hall, the Global Scholars Hall, opened in the fall of 2012. It primarily houses returning students and students enrolled in the Robert D. Clark Honors College, College Scholars, and the global scholars language programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_Scholars_Hall_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Scholars_Hall-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_campus">South campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: South campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Knight_Law_Center_(University_of_Oregon).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Knight_Law_Center_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg/220px-Knight_Law_Center_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Knight_Law_Center_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg/330px-Knight_Law_Center_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Knight_Law_Center_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg/440px-Knight_Law_Center_%28University_of_Oregon%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Knight_Law_Center_(University_of_Oregon).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Knight Law Center (University of Oregon)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The center of south campus is where much of the on-campus athletic facilities reside. <a href="/wiki/Hayward_Field" title="Hayward Field">Hayward Field</a>, home to the Ducks track and field program, sits in the eastern area of the athletic facilities. It has hosted a number of prominent track and field events such as the US Track and Field Olympic Trials, the NCAA Track and Field Championships, and <a href="/wiki/USATF" title="USATF" class="mw-redirect">USATF</a> Championships.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>To the west of the athletic facilities lies <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Pioneer_Cemetery" title="Eugene Pioneer Cemetery">Pioneer Cemetery</a> and further west is where the current facilities for the College of Education exists, in the southwest corner of campus. The HEDCO Education building and the Frohnmayer Music Center are in the vicinity. The Knight Law Center is located just opposite of Hayward Field in the southeast corner of campus. The Many Nations Longhouse and the Museum of Natural and Cultural History are East of Knight Law.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_areas_and_satellites">Other areas and satellites</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other areas and satellites">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The controversial<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Riverfront Research Park is a small facility maintained by the university, located across Franklin Boulevard from the main campus, next to the Willamette River. The park is used for creating new technologies, such as research about artificial intelligence at the Computational Intelligence Research Lab, and it is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Zebrafish_Information_Network" title="Zebrafish Information Network">Zebrafish Information Network</a> (ZFIN), the <a href="/wiki/Zebrafish" title="Zebrafish">zebrafish</a> <a href="/wiki/Model_organism" title="Model organism">model organism</a> database. Local controversy has existed since before the development and approval of the site master plan by the City of Eugene in 1989. Controversy stems from the lack of citizen involvement in the planning process for the use of public lands, and the potential for multi-story office buildings and parking lots to replace open space, civic space, and wildlife habitat along the Willamette River. The University and Student Senates have each passed resolutions<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> against construction on the banks of the Willamette River under the current development plan, yet plans for development persist. In March 2010, the issue of a conditional use permit extension for the Research Park was appealed to the Land Use Board of Appeals by a group of citizens, students, and faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The complex for the Ducks football and baseball team is located north across the Willamette River. It includes the football stadium (<a href="/wiki/Autzen_Stadium" title="Autzen Stadium">Autzen Stadium</a>),the baseball park (<a href="/wiki/PK_Park" title="PK Park">PK Park</a>), an indoor practice football field (Moshofsky Center), an outdoor practice field (Kilkenny Field), and the Casanova Center which includes offices, the athletics Hall of Fame, locker rooms, weight rooms, a film review theater, and a treatment center.</p> 
     <p>The university also leases space in Old Town Portland in the White Stag Block. UO-Portland provides an urban study environment for the School of Architecture and Allied Arts, the School of Journalism and Communication, the School of Law, and the Lundquist College of Business. Additionally, the Division of Continuing Education, the Labor Education Resource Center, and the Department of Athletics have active offices there. <a href="/wiki/The_Duck_Store" title="The Duck Store">The Duck Store</a> has an outlet in the building.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Oregon received a grade of &quot;B+&quot; from the Sustainable Endowments Institute on its College Sustainability Report Card 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The undergraduate architecture program is consistently ranked among the highest in the country, and is currently ranked as the #1 public program for &quot;Sustainable Design Practice and Principles&quot; by DesignIntelligence magazine.</p> 
     <p>There has also been a push for sustainable buildings on campus with a development plan that requires any new building or renovation to incorporate sustainable design.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lillis_Business_Complex" title="Lillis Business Complex">Lillis Business Complex</a> was the catalyst for the policy. The building, completed in 2003<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> has earned a LEED Silver rating, the highest rating of any college business building in the United States.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Product_Design_Network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Green Product Design Network (page does not exist)">Green Product Design Network</a> (GPDN) was created by a group of leaders from the UO with expertise in <a href="/wiki/Green_chemistry" title="Green chemistry">green chemistry</a>, product design, business, communications, and journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_museums">Libraries and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Libraries and museums">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UO_KnightLibrary_Front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/UO_KnightLibrary_Front.jpg/220px-UO_KnightLibrary_Front.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/UO_KnightLibrary_Front.jpg/330px-UO_KnightLibrary_Front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/UO_KnightLibrary_Front.jpg/440px-UO_KnightLibrary_Front.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UO_KnightLibrary_Front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Knight_Library" title="Knight Library">Knight Library</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The multi-branch University of Oregon Libraries serves the campus with library collections, instruction and reference, and a wide variety of educational technology and media services. The UO is Oregon's only member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Research_Libraries" title="Association of Research Libraries">Association of Research Libraries</a>. The main branch, the <a href="/wiki/Knight_Library" title="Knight Library">Knight Library</a>, houses humanities and social sciences, Learning Commons, Music Services, Government Publications, Maps and Aerial Photos, Special Collections &amp; University Archives, Media Services, the Center for Educational Technologies, and a Cinema Studies lab to be available in Winter 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Other branch locations are:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The Architecture and Allied Arts Library in Lawrence Hall</li> 
      <li>The Global Scholars Hall Library Commons in Global Scholars Hall</li> 
      <li>The John E. Jaqua Law Library in the Knight Law Center</li> 
      <li>The Loyd &amp; Dorothy Rippey Library at the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Institute_of_Marine_Biology" title="Oregon Institute of Marine Biology">Oregon Institute of Marine Biology</a> in Charleston, Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The Mathematics Library in Fenton Hall</li> 
      <li>The Portland Library &amp; Learning Commons in the White Stag Block in Portland, Oregon</li> 
      <li>The Science Library under Onyx Bridge</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><br /> The UO Libraries hosts Scholars' Bank, an <a href="/wiki/Open_access_(publishing)" title="Open access (publishing)" class="mw-redirect">open access</a> (OA) digital repository created to capture, distribute and preserve the intellectual output of the University of Oregon. Scholars' Bank uses open-source <a href="/wiki/DSpace" title="DSpace">DSpace</a> software developed by <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>.</p> 
     <p>The Libraries' Educational Video Group maintains the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://media.uoregon.edu/channel/">UO Channel</a>, which uses streaming media to provide access to campus lectures, interviews, performances, symposia, and documentary productions.</p> 
     <p>The UO is the founding member and host of the <a href="/wiki/Orbis_Cascade_Alliance" title="Orbis Cascade Alliance">Orbis-Cascade Alliance</a>, a consortium of academic and research libraries in Oregon,Washington and Idaho. The combined collections of the Alliance exceed 20 million volumes and can be searched via the Summit union catalog. The Orbis Cascade Alliance serves faculty and the equivalent of more than 258,000 full-time students. In addition to its members, the Alliance extends selected services to more than 280 libraries, museums, archives, and historical societies in seven western states.</p> 
     <p>The University of Oregon is home to the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Schnitzer_Museum_of_Art" title="Jordan Schnitzer Museum of Art">Jordan Schnitzer Museum of Art</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_Museum_of_Natural_and_Cultural_History" title="University of Oregon Museum of Natural and Cultural History">Museum of Natural and Cultural History</a>.</p> 
     <p>There are multiple galleries around the main campus, including (but not limited to):</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The LaVerne Krause Gallery in Lawrence Hall</li> 
      <li>The Adell McMillan Gallery in the Erb Memorial Union</li> 
      <li>The Aperture Gallery in the Erb Memorial Union</li> 
      <li>The art gallery on the second floor of the Knight Law Center</li> 
      <li>The Washburn Gallery in the FAS Ceramics building.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life_and_culture">Student life and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Student life and culture">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Representation">Representation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Representation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Asuo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Asuo.JPG/220px-Asuo.JPG" width="220" height="77" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Asuo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Asuo.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Asuo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Associated_Students_of_the_University_of_Oregon_(ASUO)" title="Associated Students of the University of Oregon (ASUO)" class="mw-redirect">ASUO</a> Window Sign, EMU Suite 4
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Students_of_the_University_of_Oregon_(ASUO)" title="Associated Students of the University of Oregon (ASUO)" class="mw-redirect">Associated Students of the University of Oregon (ASUO)</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Student_government" title="Student government" class="mw-redirect">student government</a> at the University of Oregon. It is a non-profit organization funded by the University of Oregon. Its purpose is to provide for the <a href="/wiki/Social" title="Social">social</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cultural" title="Cultural" class="mw-redirect">cultural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">educational</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_body" title="Human body">physical</a> development of its members, and for the advancement of their individual and collective interests both within and without the University. The ASUO is the <a href="/wiki/Student_government" title="Student government" class="mw-redirect">student government</a> and is run by students for students and works on <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_campus" title="University of Oregon campus" class="mw-redirect">campus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eugene,_Oregon" title="Eugene, Oregon">city</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">state</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">federal</a>-level <a href="/wiki/Political_campaign" title="Political campaign">campaigns</a>. Membership consists of all students at the University of Oregon, <a href="/wiki/Eugene,_Oregon" title="Eugene, Oregon">Eugene, Oregon</a>, who have paid the current term or <a href="/wiki/Semester" title="Semester" class="mw-redirect">semester</a> student incidental fee.<sup id="cite_ref-info_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-info-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Additionally, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Erb_Memorial_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Erb Memorial Union (page does not exist)">Erb Memorial Union</a> <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Directors" title="Board of Directors" class="mw-redirect">Board of Directors</a> is responsible for making general policy decisions and long-range plans for the operation of the EMU. The board allocates the EMU's multi-million dollar <a href="/wiki/Budget" title="Budget">budget</a>, assigns space for student groups and advises staff in the <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">management</a> of the EMU. The sixteen-member <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Directors" title="Board of Directors" class="mw-redirect">Board</a> consists of twelve students (seven elected in a campus-wide election and five direct appointments from either EMU programs or the ASUO), three faculty members appointed by the University of Oregon President and one EMU staff member elected by their peers.<sup id="cite_ref-EMUBoardinfo_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMUBoardinfo-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Every fiscal year, the EMU Board prepares a benchmark increase to the ASUO Senate for approval. After the benchmark process, the EMU presents its final budget to the Senate, requesting a decrease, increase, or no change in Incidental Fees to be allocated to the EMU. If the budget request is approved, the budget must be signed by the ASUO President and then the UO President. Unlike the budget process, any general policy decisions by the EMU Board do not require Senate oversight or approval.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities_and_housing">Facilities and housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Facilities and housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Living-Learning_Center_North_(LLC_North).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Living-Learning_Center_North_%28LLC_North%29.jpg/220px-Living-Learning_Center_North_%28LLC_North%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Living-Learning_Center_North_%28LLC_North%29.jpg/330px-Living-Learning_Center_North_%28LLC_North%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Living-Learning_Center_North_%28LLC_North%29.jpg/440px-Living-Learning_Center_North_%28LLC_North%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Living-Learning_Center_North_(LLC_North).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The north building of the Living-Learning Center housing complex at the University of Oregon, opened in 2006
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Erb Memorial Union (EMU) is the student union, which provides many various student life amenities and sits on the southeast corner of 13th and University. It contains a food court, restaurants and cafes, student groups, meeting rooms and performance spaces, the campus radio station 88.1 KWVA, the Break Pool Hall, and offices for administration. South of the Erb Memorial Union across a small quad is the Student Recreational Center (SRC) which is an exercise and recreation facility. It includes fitness equipment, rock climbing walls, a swimming pool, racquetball courts, an indoor elevated running track and basketball courts. Covered tennis courts and several turf fields, and outdoor tennis courts within a running track are located near the recreation center.</p> 
     <p>There is currently a proposal to renovate and expand the EMU, as well as the SRC. This proposal includes a 1500 seat concert hall. The $161 million project's designs are expected to be completed by April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Erb_Memorial_Union_Expansion_and_Renovation_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erb_Memorial_Union_Expansion_and_Renovation-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> However, its current construction timeline is uncertain, as some members of the ASUO have voiced concerns about the project.<sup id="cite_ref-Student_facility_remodels_in_flux_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Student_facility_remodels_in_flux-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>There are nine Residence Halls: Barnhart, Bean, Carson, Earl, the Global Scholars Hall, Hamilton, the Living-Learning Center, Riley, and Walton.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The Global Scholars Hall was opened in the Fall of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> This 451-bed student housing facility is part of the university's plan to increase total undergraduate enrollment to 24,000 students in the near future.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>There are more than 250 student groups at the University of Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon_media" title="University of Oregon media">University of Oregon media</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Oregon has a diverse array of student-run and student-created media, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Oregon_Daily_Emerald" title="Oregon Daily Emerald" class="mw-redirect">Oregon Daily Emerald</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Oregon_Commentator" title="Oregon Commentator">Oregon Commentator</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Ethos_Magazine" title="Ethos Magazine">Ethos Magazine</a></i> among others<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Libraries' Educational Video Group maintains the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://media.uoregon.edu/channel/">UO Channel</a>, which uses streaming media to provide access to campus lectures, interviews, performances, symposia, and documentary productions.</p> 
     <p>The University is also home of two radio stations: <a href="/wiki/KWAX" title="KWAX">KWAX</a> (<a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a>) and <a href="/wiki/KWVA" title="KWVA">KWVA</a> (<a href="/wiki/Campus_radio" title="Campus radio">campus radio</a>).</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Forensics">Forensics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Forensics">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>In addition to its athletic teams, the university also has a competitive intercollegiate <a href="/wiki/Individual_Events" title="Individual Events" class="mw-redirect">Speech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Debate" title="Debate">Debate</a> team. The University of Oregon Forensics program was founded in 1876, at the same time as the university. Initially the program consisted of two student-formed forensic societies, which developed into &quot;doughnut league&quot; inter-dorm competitions in the 1890s. In 1891, the UO began intercollegiate competition. Forensics continued to grow as a staple of the university's community and by 1911, the team was so successful that it began charging admission to debates. Money raised during these events was often donated to the fledgling University of Oregon football program.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/National_Parliamentary_Debate_Association" title="National Parliamentary Debate Association">Parliamentary debate</a> was integrated into UO Forensics in 1998–99 and the team has been competitive since. In 2001, the UO's Alan Tauber and Heidi Ford claimed a national title, winning the first ever <a href="/wiki/National_Parliamentary_Tournament_of_Excellence" title="National Parliamentary Tournament of Excellence">National Parliamentary Tournament of Excellence</a> (NPTE). In 2011, the team of Matt Gander and Hank Fields claimed both national titles, winning the NPTE and the <a href="/wiki/National_Parliamentary_Debate_Association" title="National Parliamentary Debate Association">National Parliamentary Debate Association</a> Championship, coached by Thomas Schally, Benjamin Dodds, Sarah Hamid, and Will Chamberlain.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <ul> 
      <li>A cappella groups perform at the venue in front of the EMU on Friday afternoons.</li> 
      <li>&quot;It never rains at Autzen stadium.&quot; – It is a tradition for the announcer to call this out sometime during each football game.</li> 
      <li>Street Fair – Twice a year, a street fair lines the entire stretch of the University of Oregon campus on 13th Street. It features exceptional food and plenty of arts and crafts.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Ducks" title="Oregon Ducks">Oregon Ducks</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Jaquacenterwet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Jaquacenterwet.jpg/220px-Jaquacenterwet.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Jaquacenterwet.jpg/330px-Jaquacenterwet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Jaquacenterwet.jpg/440px-Jaquacenterwet.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Jaquacenterwet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Jaqua_Center" title="Jaqua Center" class="mw-redirect">John E. Jaqua Center for Student Athletes</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Oregon is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> Football Bowl Subdivision of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>. The athletic programs have garnered 21 NCAA team championships,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as 60 NCAA individual champions in various track and field events.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The two primary rivals of the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Ducks_football" title="Oregon Ducks football">Oregon Ducks football</a> team are the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies" title="Washington Huskies">Washington Huskies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_Beavers" title="Oregon State Beavers">Oregon State Beavers</a>. The football rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_University" title="Oregon State University">Oregon State University</a>, known as the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Civil_War_(college_football_game)" title="Civil War (college football game)">Civil War</a>&quot;, is one of the nation's oldest. Every year, the two teams face off in the last game of the regular season. The two teams have faced each other nearly every year since 1894 with the exception of five years. Games were not held in 1900, 1901, 1911, 1943, and 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-UpCloseAndPersonal_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UpCloseAndPersonal-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university competes in 14 sports: football, men’s and women’s basketball, cross country, track and field, baseball, softball, men’s and women’s tennis, men’s and women’s golf, women’s soccer, women’s lacrosse, women’s volleyball, and acrobatics &amp; tumbling. This does not include club sports which competes at the Division I level in Rugby, Soccer, Rowing, and Waterpolo. As well as women's Division I club athletics in Rowing, Rugby, and Waterpolo.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:143px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:OregonDucks.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/OregonDucks.svg/141px-OregonDucks.svg.png" width="141" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/OregonDucks.svg/212px-OregonDucks.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/OregonDucks.svg/282px-OregonDucks.svg.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:OregonDucks.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <i>UO Athletics Logo</i>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>With 20 NCAA championships between them, cross country and track and field are the two programs at the university that have enjoyed the most success. The programs have produced many world-class athletes including <a href="/wiki/Steve_Prefontaine" title="Steve Prefontaine">Steve Prefontaine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Salazar" title="Alberto Salazar">Alberto Salazar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc" title="Nike, Inc" class="mw-redirect">Nike</a> had been formed by the former track and field head coach <a href="/wiki/Bill_Bowerman" title="Bill Bowerman">Bill Bowerman</a> and former University of Oregon track runner <a href="/wiki/Phil_Knight" title="Phil Knight">Phil Knight</a>. The successes of the programs have given the name of Track Town, USA to Eugene.</p> 
     <p>Created in 1893, the football team played its first game in 1894 and won its first <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(game)" title="Rose Bowl (game)" class="mw-redirect">Rose Bowl</a> in 1917 against the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>. The 1938–39 men's basketball team, nicknamed the “Tall Firs,” won the first-ever NCAA basketball tournament by defeating <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State" title="Ohio State" class="mw-redirect">Ohio State</a> in the March 28, 1939 championship game.<sup id="cite_ref-UOAthTimeline_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UOAthTimeline-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Originally recognized as an official sport at the university in 1908, baseball was disbanded in 1981 due to concerns with <a href="/wiki/Title_IX" title="Title IX">Title IX</a>. In 2007, the athletic director <a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kilkenny&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Patrick Kilkenny (page does not exist)">Patrick Kilkenny</a> announced plans to reinstate baseball and to drop wrestling while adding women’s acrobatics &amp; tumbling.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/The_Oregon_Duck" title="The Oregon Duck">The Oregon Duck</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The mascot of the University of Oregon is the fighting duck. The popular <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">Disney</a> character <a href="/wiki/Donald_Duck" title="Donald Duck">Donald Duck</a> has been the mascot for decades, thanks to a handshake agreement made between then-Athletic Director <a href="/wiki/Leo_Harris" title="Leo Harris">Leo Harris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walt Disney</a> in 1947.<sup id="cite_ref-MascotHistory_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MascotHistory-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The mascot has been challenged more than a few times in its lifetime. The first came in 1966 when Walt Disney died and the company realized there was no formal contract written for the use of Donald’s image. A formal contract was written up in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-MascotHistory_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MascotHistory-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Potential heirs &quot;Mallard Drake&quot; and &quot;Mandrake&quot; challenged Donald’s position in 1978 and 2003 respectively,<sup id="cite_ref-MascotHistory_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MascotHistory-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> but both were unpopular and discontinued.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Song">Song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Song">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Mighty_Oregon" title="Mighty Oregon">Mighty Oregon</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> is &quot;<a href="/wiki/Mighty_Oregon" title="Mighty Oregon">Mighty Oregon</a>&quot;, written by student Albert Perfect and professor John DeWitt Gilbert in 1916. It has undergone several changes since its original performance.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_fiction_and_popular_culture">In fiction and popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: In fiction and popular culture">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Onscreen">Onscreen</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oregon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Onscreen">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The film <i><a href="/wiki/National_Lampoon%27s_Animal_House" title="National Lampoon's Animal House">National Lampoon's Animal House</a></i> (1978) was filmed on the university campus and the surrounding area. The building used as the exterior of the Delta House (which belonged to the University of Oregon <a href="/wiki/Pi_Kappa_Alpha" title="Pi Kappa Alpha">Pi Kappa Alpha</a> chapter) was demolished in 1986, but the interior scenes were shot in the <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Nu" title="Sigma Nu">Sigma Nu</a> house, which still stands today. The Omega house belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Psi" title="Phi Kappa Psi">Phi Kappa Psi</a> fraternity and still stands today. The sorority house where Bluto climbs the ladder to peek in on the coeds was actually the exterior of the Sigma Nu fraternity.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Other buildings that were used during filming include Johnson Hall, Gerlinger Hall, Fenton Hall, Carson Hall, and the Erb Memorial Union (EMU). The EMU dining facility known as &quot;The Fishbowl&quot; was the site of the famous food-fight scene. The Knight Library and the Jordan Schnitzer Museum of Art can also be seen in the movie.<sup id="cite_ref-film_sites_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-film_sites-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Other films shot at the university include</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Abe_Lincoln_in_Illinois_(film)" title="Abe Lincoln in Illinois (film)">Abe Lincoln in Illinois</a></i> (1940)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Five_Easy_Pieces" title="Five Easy Pieces">Five Easy Pieces</a></i> (1970)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Drive,_He_Said" title="Drive, He Said">Drive, He Said</a></i> (1970)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/How_to_Beat_the_High_Cost_of_Living" title="How to Beat the High Cost of Living" class="mw-redirect">How to Beat the High Cost of Living</a></i> (1980)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Personal_Best_(film)" title="Personal Best (film)">Personal Best</a></i> (1982)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Stand_by_Me_(film)" title="Stand by Me (film)">Stand By Me</a></i> (1986) (shot primarily in nearby <a href="/wiki/Brownsville,_Oregon" title="Brownsville, Oregon">Brownsville, Oregon</a>)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Without_Limits" title="Without Limits">Without Limits</a></i> (1998)</li> 
     </ul>
